[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jimmy_Wales_in_France%2C_with_the_style_of_Munch%27s_%22The_Scream%22_applied_using_neural_style_transfer.jpg/250px-Jimmy_Wales_in_France%2C_with_the_style_of_Munch%27s_%22The_Scream%22_applied_using_neural_style_transfer.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/File:Jimmy_Wales_in_France,_with_the_style_of_Munch%27s_%22The_Scream%22_applied_using_neural_style_transfer.jpg>)Visual art processing of Jimmy Wales in France, with the style of Munch's "[The Scream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/The_Scream> "The Scream")" applied using neural style transfer
Closely related to the progress that has been made in image recognition is the increasing application of deep learning techniques to various visual art tasks. DNNs have proven themselves capable, for example, of 
  * identifying the style period of a given painting[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art1-189>)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art2-190>)
  * [Neural Style Transfer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Neural_Style_Transfer> "Neural Style Transfer") – capturing the style of a given artwork and applying it in a visually pleasing manner to an arbitrary photograph or video[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art1-189>)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art2-190>)
  * generating striking imagery based on random visual input fields.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art1-189>)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-art2-190>)


### Natural language processing
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=16> "Edit section: Natural language processing")]
Main article: [Natural language processing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Natural_language_processing> "Natural language processing")
Neural networks have been used for implementing language models since the early 2000s.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-gers2001-150>) LSTM helped to improve machine translation and language modeling.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-NIPS2014-151>)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-vinyals2016-152>)[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-gillick2015-153>)
Other key techniques in this field are negative sampling[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-GoldbergLevy2014-191>) and [word embedding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Word_embedding> "Word embedding"). Word embedding, such as _[word2vec](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Word2vec> "Word2vec")_ , can be thought of as a representational layer in a deep learning architecture that transforms an atomic word into a positional representation of the word relative to other words in the dataset; the position is represented as a point in a [vector space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Vector_space> "Vector space"). Using word embedding as an RNN input layer allows the network to parse sentences and phrases using an effective compositional vector grammar. A compositional vector grammar can be thought of as [probabilistic context free grammar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Probabilistic_context_free_grammar> "Probabilistic context free grammar") (PCFG) implemented by an RNN.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-SocherManning2014-192>) Recursive auto-encoders built atop word embeddings can assess sentence similarity and detect paraphrasing.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-SocherManning2014-192>) Deep neural architectures provide the best results for constituency parsing,[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-193>) [sentiment analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Sentiment_analysis> "Sentiment analysis"),[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-RDM_1-194>) information retrieval,[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-195>)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-196>) spoken language understanding,[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-IEEE-TASL2015-197>) machine translation,[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-NIPS2014-151>)[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-auto-198>) contextual entity linking,[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-auto-198>) writing style recognition,[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-BROC2017-199>) [named-entity recognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Named-entity_recognition> "Named-entity recognition") (token classification),[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-200>) text classification, and others.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-201>)
Recent developments generalize [word embedding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Word_embedding> "Word embedding") to [sentence embedding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Sentence_embedding> "Sentence embedding"). 
[Google Translate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Google_Translate> "Google Translate") (GT) uses a large end-to-end [long short-term memory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Long_short-term_memory> "Long short-term memory") (LSTM) network.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-GT_Turovsky_2016-202>)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-googleblog_GNMT_2016-203>)[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-GoogleTranslate-204>)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-WiredGoogleTranslate-205>) [Google Neural Machine Translation (GNMT)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Google_Neural_Machine_Translation> "Google Neural Machine Translation") uses an [example-based machine translation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Example-based_machine_translation> "Example-based machine translation") method in which the system "learns from millions of examples".[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-googleblog_GNMT_2016-203>) It translates "whole sentences at a time, rather than pieces". Google Translate supports over one hundred languages.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-googleblog_GNMT_2016-203>) The network encodes the "semantics of the sentence rather than simply memorizing phrase-to-phrase translations".[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-googleblog_GNMT_2016-203>)[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Biotet-206>) GT uses English as an intermediate between most language pairs.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Biotet-206>)
### Drug discovery and toxicology
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=17> "Edit section: Drug discovery and toxicology")]
For more information, see [Drug discovery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Drug_discovery> "Drug discovery") and [Toxicology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Toxicology> "Toxicology").
A large percentage of candidate drugs fail to win regulatory approval. These failures are caused by insufficient efficacy (on-target effect), undesired interactions (off-target effects), or unanticipated [toxic effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Toxicity> "Toxicity").[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-ARROWSMITH2013-207>)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-VERBIEST2015-208>) Research has explored use of deep learning to predict the [biomolecular targets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Biomolecular_target> "Biomolecular target"),[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-MERCK2012-209>)[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:5-210>) [off-targets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Off-target> "Off-target"), and [toxic effects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Toxicity> "Toxicity") of environmental chemicals in nutrients, household products and drugs.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-TOX21-211>)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-TOX21Data-212>)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:11-213>)
AtomNet is a deep learning system for structure-based [rational drug design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Drug_design> "Drug design").[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-214>) AtomNet was used to predict novel candidate biomolecules for disease targets such as the [Ebola virus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Ebola_virus> "Ebola virus")[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Toronto-215>) and [multiple sclerosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Multiple_sclerosis> "Multiple sclerosis").[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-216>)[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Toronto-215>)
In 2017 [graph neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Graph_neural_network> "Graph neural network") were used for the first time to predict various properties of molecules in a large toxicology data set.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-217>) In 2019, generative neural networks were used to produce molecules that were validated experimentally all the way into mice.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-218>)[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-219>)
### Customer relationship management
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=18> "Edit section: Customer relationship management")]
Main article: [Customer relationship management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Customer_relationship_management> "Customer relationship management")
[Deep reinforcement learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deep_reinforcement_learning> "Deep reinforcement learning") has been used to approximate the value of possible [direct marketing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Direct_marketing> "Direct marketing") actions, defined in terms of [RFM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/RFM_\(customer_value\)> "RFM \(customer value\)") variables. The estimated value function was shown to have a natural interpretation as [customer lifetime value](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Customer_lifetime_value> "Customer lifetime value").[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-220>)
### Recommendation systems
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=19> "Edit section: Recommendation systems")]
Main article: [Recommender system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Recommender_system> "Recommender system")
Recommendation systems have used deep learning to extract meaningful features for a latent factor model for content-based music and journal recommendations.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-221>)[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-222>) Multi-view deep learning has been applied for learning user preferences from multiple domains.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-223>) The model uses a hybrid collaborative and content-based approach and enhances recommendations in multiple tasks. 
### Bioinformatics
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=20> "Edit section: Bioinformatics")]
Main article: [Bioinformatics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Bioinformatics> "Bioinformatics")
An [autoencoder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Autoencoder> "Autoencoder") ANN was used in [bioinformatics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Bioinformatics> "Bioinformatics"), to predict [gene ontology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Gene_Ontology> "Gene Ontology") annotations and gene-function relationships.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-224>)
In medical informatics, deep learning was used to predict sleep quality based on data from wearables[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-225>) and predictions of health complications from [electronic health record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Electronic_health_record> "Electronic health record") data.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-226>)
Deep neural networks have shown unparalleled performance in [predicting protein structure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Protein_structure_prediction> "Protein structure prediction"), according to the sequence of the amino acids that make it up. In 2020, [AlphaFold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/AlphaFold> "AlphaFold"), a deep-learning based system, achieved a level of accuracy significantly higher than all previous computational methods.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-227>)[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-228>)
### Deep Neural Network Estimations
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=21> "Edit section: Deep Neural Network Estimations")]
Deep neural networks can be used to estimate the entropy of a [stochastic process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Stochastic_process> "Stochastic process") and called Neural Joint Entropy Estimator (NJEE).[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-SPB22-229>) Such an estimation provides insights on the effects of input [random variables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Random_variables> "Random variables") on an independent [random variable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Random_variable> "Random variable"). Practically, the DNN is trained as a [classifier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Classifier_\(machine_learning\)> "Classifier \(machine learning\)") that maps an input [vector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Vector_\(mathematics_and_physics\)> "Vector \(mathematics and physics\)") or [matrix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Matrix_\(mathematics\)> "Matrix \(mathematics\)") X to an output [probability distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Probability_distribution> "Probability distribution") over the possible classes of random variable Y, given input X. For example, in [image classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Image_classification> "Image classification") tasks, the NJEE maps a vector of [pixels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Pixels> "Pixels")' color values to probabilities over possible image classes. In practice, the probability distribution of Y is obtained by a [Softmax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Softmax> "Softmax") layer with number of nodes that is equal to the [alphabet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Alphabet> "Alphabet") size of Y. NJEE uses continuously differentiable [activation functions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Activation_function> "Activation function"), such that the conditions for the [universal approximation theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Universal_approximation_theorem> "Universal approximation theorem") holds. It is shown that this method provides a strongly [consistent estimator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Consistent_estimator> "Consistent estimator") and outperforms other methods in case of large alphabet sizes.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-SPB22-229>)
### Medical image analysis
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=22> "Edit section: Medical image analysis")]
Deep learning has been shown to produce competitive results in medical application such as cancer cell classification, lesion detection, organ segmentation and image enhancement.[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-230>)[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-231>) Modern deep learning tools demonstrate the high accuracy of detecting various diseases and the helpfulness of their use by specialists to improve the diagnosis efficiency.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-232>)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-233>)
### Mobile advertising
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=23> "Edit section: Mobile advertising")]
Finding the appropriate mobile audience for [mobile advertising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Mobile_advertising> "Mobile advertising") is always challenging, since many data points must be considered and analyzed before a target segment can be created and used in ad serving by any ad server.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-234>) Deep learning has been used to interpret large, many-dimensioned advertising datasets. Many data points are collected during the request/serve/click internet advertising cycle. This information can form the basis of machine learning to improve ad selection. 
### Image restoration
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=24> "Edit section: Image restoration")]
Deep learning has been successfully applied to [inverse problems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Inverse_problems> "Inverse problems") such as [denoising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Denoising> "Denoising"), [super-resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Super-resolution> "Super-resolution"), [inpainting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Inpainting> "Inpainting"), and [film colorization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Film_colorization> "Film colorization").[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-235>) These applications include learning methods such as "Shrinkage Fields for Effective Image Restoration"[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-236>) which trains on an image dataset, and [Deep Image Prior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deep_Image_Prior> "Deep Image Prior"), which trains on the image that needs restoration. 
### Financial fraud detection
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=25> "Edit section: Financial fraud detection")]
Deep learning is being successfully applied to financial [fraud detection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Fraud_detection> "Fraud detection"), tax evasion detection,[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-237>) and anti-money laundering.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-238>)
### Materials science
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=26> "Edit section: Materials science")]
In November 2023, researchers at [Google DeepMind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Google_DeepMind> "Google DeepMind") and [Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Lawrence_Berkeley_National_Laboratory> "Lawrence Berkeley National Laboratory") announced that they had developed an AI system known as GNoME. This system has contributed to [materials science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Materials_science> "Materials science") by discovering over 2 million new materials within a relatively short timeframe. GNoME employs deep learning techniques to efficiently explore potential material structures, achieving a significant increase in the identification of stable inorganic [crystal structures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Crystal_structure> "Crystal structure"). The system's predictions were validated through autonomous robotic experiments, demonstrating a noteworthy success rate of 71%. The data of newly discovered materials is publicly available through the [Materials Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Materials_Project> "Materials Project") database, offering researchers the opportunity to identify materials with desired properties for various applications. This development has implications for the future of scientific discovery and the integration of AI in material science research, potentially expediting material innovation and reducing costs in product development. The use of AI and deep learning suggests the possibility of minimizing or eliminating manual lab experiments and allowing scientists to focus more on the design and analysis of unique compounds.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-239>)[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-240>)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-241>)
### Military
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=27> "Edit section: Military")]
The United States Department of Defense applied deep learning to train robots in new tasks through observation.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:12-242>)
### Partial differential equations
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=28> "Edit section: Partial differential equations")]
Physics informed neural networks have been used to solve [partial differential equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Partial_differential_equation> "Partial differential equation") in both forward and inverse problems in a data driven manner.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-243>) One example is the reconstructing fluid flow governed by the [Navier-Stokes equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Navier%E2%80%93Stokes_equations> "Navier–Stokes equations"). Using physics informed neural networks does not require the often expensive mesh generation that conventional [CFD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Computational_fluid_dynamics> "Computational fluid dynamics") methods rely on.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-244>)[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-245>)
### Deep backward stochastic differential equation method
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=29> "Edit section: Deep backward stochastic differential equation method")]
[Deep backward stochastic differential equation method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deep_backward_stochastic_differential_equation_method> "Deep backward stochastic differential equation method") is a numerical method that combines deep learning with [Backward stochastic differential equation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Backward_stochastic_differential_equation> "Backward stochastic differential equation") (BSDE). This method is particularly useful for solving high-dimensional problems in financial mathematics. By leveraging the powerful function approximation capabilities of [deep neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deep_neural_networks> "Deep neural networks"), deep BSDE addresses the computational challenges faced by traditional numerical methods in high-dimensional settings. Specifically, traditional methods like finite difference methods or Monte Carlo simulations often struggle with the curse of dimensionality, where computational cost increases exponentially with the number of dimensions. Deep BSDE methods, however, employ deep neural networks to approximate solutions of high-dimensional partial differential equations (PDEs), effectively reducing the computational burden.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Han2018-246>)
In addition, the integration of [Physics-informed neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Physics-informed_neural_networks> "Physics-informed neural networks") (PINNs) into the deep BSDE framework enhances its capability by embedding the underlying physical laws directly into the neural network architecture. This ensures that the solutions not only fit the data but also adhere to the governing stochastic differential equations. PINNs leverage the power of deep learning while respecting the constraints imposed by the physical models, resulting in more accurate and reliable solutions for financial mathematics problems. 
### Image reconstruction
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=30> "Edit section: Image reconstruction")]
Image reconstruction is the reconstruction of the underlying images from the image-related measurements. Several works showed the better and superior performance of the deep learning methods compared to analytical methods for various applications, e.g., spectral imaging [[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-247>) and ultrasound imaging.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-248>)
### Weather prediction
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=31> "Edit section: Weather prediction")]
Traditional weather prediction systems solve a very complex system of partial differential equations. GraphCast is a deep learning based model, trained on a long history of weather data to predict how weather patterns change over time. It is able to predict weather conditions for up to 10 days globally, at a very detailed level, and in under a minute, with precision similar to state of the art systems.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-249>)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-250>)
### Epigenetic clock
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=32> "Edit section: Epigenetic clock")]
Main article: [Epigenetic clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Epigenetic_clock> "Epigenetic clock")
An epigenetic clock is a [biochemical test](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Biomarkers_of_aging> "Biomarkers of aging") that can be used to measure age. Galkin et al. used deep neural networks to train an epigenetic aging clock of unprecedented accuracy using >6,000 blood samples.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-251>) The clock uses information from 1000 [CpG sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/CpG_site> "CpG site") and predicts people with certain conditions older than healthy controls: [IBD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Inflammatory_bowel_disease> "Inflammatory bowel disease"), [frontotemporal dementia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Frontotemporal_dementia> "Frontotemporal dementia"), [ovarian cancer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Ovarian_cancer> "Ovarian cancer"), [obesity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Obesity> "Obesity"). The aging clock was planned to be released for public use in 2021 by an [Insilico Medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Insilico_Medicine> "Insilico Medicine") spinoff company Deep Longevity. 
## Relation to human cognitive and brain development
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=33> "Edit section: Relation to human cognitive and brain development")]
Deep learning is closely related to a class of theories of [brain development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Brain_development> "Brain development") (specifically, neocortical development) proposed by [cognitive neuroscientists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Cognitive_neuroscientist> "Cognitive neuroscientist") in the early 1990s.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-UTGOFF-252>)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-ELMAN-253>)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-SHRAGER-254>)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-QUARTZ-255>) These developmental theories were instantiated in computational models, making them predecessors of deep learning systems. These developmental models share the property that various proposed learning dynamics in the brain (e.g., a wave of [nerve growth factor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Nerve_growth_factor> "Nerve growth factor")) support the [self-organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Self-organization> "Self-organization") somewhat analogous to the neural networks utilized in deep learning models. Like the [neocortex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Neocortex> "Neocortex"), neural networks employ a hierarchy of layered filters in which each layer considers information from a prior layer (or the operating environment), and then passes its output (and possibly the original input), to other layers. This process yields a self-organizing stack of [transducers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Transducer> "Transducer"), well-tuned to their operating environment. A 1995 description stated, "...the infant's brain seems to organize itself under the influence of waves of so-called trophic-factors ... different regions of the brain become connected sequentially, with one layer of tissue maturing before another and so on until the whole brain is mature".[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-BLAKESLEE-256>)
A variety of approaches have been used to investigate the plausibility of deep learning models from a neurobiological perspective. On the one hand, several variants of the [backpropagation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Backpropagation> "Backpropagation") algorithm have been proposed in order to increase its processing realism.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-257>)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-258>) Other researchers have argued that unsupervised forms of deep learning, such as those based on hierarchical [generative models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Generative_model> "Generative model") and [deep belief networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deep_belief_network> "Deep belief network"), may be closer to biological reality.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-259>)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-260>) In this respect, generative neural network models have been related to neurobiological evidence about sampling-based processing in the cerebral cortex.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-261>)
Although a systematic comparison between the human brain organization and the neuronal encoding in deep networks has not yet been established, several analogies have been reported. For example, the computations performed by deep learning units could be similar to those of actual neurons[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-262>) and neural populations.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-263>) Similarly, the representations developed by deep learning models are similar to those measured in the primate visual system[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-264>) both at the single-unit[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-265>) and at the population[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-266>) levels. 
## Commercial activity
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=34> "Edit section: Commercial activity")]
[Facebook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Facebook> "Facebook")'s AI lab performs tasks such as [automatically tagging uploaded pictures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Automatic_image_annotation> "Automatic image annotation") with the names of the people in them.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-METZ2013-267>)
Google's [DeepMind Technologies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/DeepMind_Technologies> "DeepMind Technologies") developed a system capable of learning how to play [Atari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Atari> "Atari") video games using only pixels as data input. In 2015 they demonstrated their [AlphaGo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/AlphaGo> "AlphaGo") system, which learned the game of [Go](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Go_\(game\)> "Go \(game\)") well enough to beat a professional Go player.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-268>)[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-269>)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-270>) [Google Translate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Google_Translate> "Google Translate") uses a neural network to translate between more than 100 languages. 
In 2017, Covariant.ai was launched, which focuses on integrating deep learning into factories.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-271>)
As of 2008,[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-272>) researchers at [The University of Texas at Austin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin> "University of Texas at Austin") (UT) developed a machine learning framework called Training an Agent Manually via Evaluative Reinforcement, or TAMER, which proposed new methods for robots or computer programs to learn how to perform tasks by interacting with a human instructor.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:12-242>) First developed as TAMER, a new algorithm called Deep TAMER was later introduced in 2018 during a collaboration between [U.S. Army Research Laboratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/U.S._Army_Research_Laboratory> "U.S. Army Research Laboratory") (ARL) and UT researchers. Deep TAMER used deep learning to provide a robot with the ability to learn new tasks through observation.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:12-242>) Using Deep TAMER, a robot learned a task with a human trainer, watching video streams or observing a human perform a task in-person. The robot later practiced the task with the help of some coaching from the trainer, who provided feedback such as "good job" and "bad job".[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-273>)
## Criticism and comment
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=35> "Edit section: Criticism and comment")]
Deep learning has attracted both criticism and comment, in some cases from outside the field of computer science. 
### Theory
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=36> "Edit section: Theory")]
See also: [Explainable artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Explainable_artificial_intelligence> "Explainable artificial intelligence")
A main criticism concerns the lack of theory surrounding some methods.[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-274>) Learning in the most common deep architectures is implemented using well-understood gradient descent. However, the theory surrounding other algorithms, such as contrastive divergence is less clear.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed> "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] (e.g., Does it converge? If so, how fast? What is it approximating?) Deep learning methods are often looked at as a [black box](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Black_box> "Black box"), with most confirmations done empirically, rather than theoretically.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-Knight_2017-275>)
In further reference to the idea that artistic sensitivity might be inherent in relatively low levels of the cognitive hierarchy, a published series of graphic representations of the internal states of deep (20-30 layers) neural networks attempting to discern within essentially random data the images on which they were trained[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-276>) demonstrate a visual appeal: the original research notice received well over 1,000 comments, and was the subject of what was for a time the most frequently accessed article on _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/The_Guardian> "The Guardian")'s_[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-277>) website. 
Furthermore, some researchers have argued that standard loss functions and differentiable architectures in deep learning may limit the discovery of deeper causal or generative mechanisms.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-278>) Building on [Algorithmic information theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Algorithmic_information_theory> "Algorithmic information theory") (AIT), Hernández-Orozco et al. (2021)[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-HernandezOrozco2021-279>) proposed an algorithmic loss function to measure the discrepancy between predicted and observed system behavior. Their approach integrates AIT with [Machine learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Machine_learning> "Machine learning") to formulate a framework for learning generative rules in non-differentiable spaces, bridging discrete algorithmic theory with continuous optimization techniques. This framework provides a new perspective on generalization and model interpretability by grounding learning dynamics in algorithmic complexity. [[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-280>) [[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-281>)
### Errors
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=37> "Edit section: Errors")]
Some deep learning architectures display problematic behaviors,[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-goertzel-282>) such as confidently classifying unrecognizable images as belonging to a familiar category of ordinary images (2014)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-283>) and misclassifying minuscule perturbations of correctly classified images (2013).[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-284>) [Goertzel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Ben_Goertzel> "Ben Goertzel") hypothesized that these behaviors are due to limitations in their internal representations and that these limitations would inhibit integration into heterogeneous multi-component [artificial general intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Artificial_general_intelligence> "Artificial general intelligence") (AGI) architectures.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-goertzel-282>) These issues may possibly be addressed by deep learning architectures that internally form states homologous to image-grammar[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-285>) decompositions of observed entities and events.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-goertzel-282>) [Learning a grammar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Grammar_induction> "Grammar induction") (visual or linguistic) from training data would be equivalent to restricting the system to [commonsense reasoning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Commonsense_reasoning> "Commonsense reasoning") that operates on concepts in terms of grammatical [production rules](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Production_\(computer_science\)> "Production \(computer science\)") and is a basic goal of both human language acquisition[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-286>) and [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Artificial_intelligence> "Artificial intelligence") (AI).[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-287>)
### Cyber threat
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=38> "Edit section: Cyber threat")]
As deep learning moves from the lab into the world, research and experience show that artificial neural networks are vulnerable to hacks and deception.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-288>) By identifying patterns that these systems use to function, attackers can modify inputs to ANNs in such a way that the ANN finds a match that human observers would not recognize. For example, an attacker can make subtle changes to an image such that the ANN finds a match even though the image looks to a human nothing like the search target. Such manipulation is termed an "[adversarial attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Adversarial_machine_learning> "Adversarial machine learning")".[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-289>)
In 2016 researchers used one ANN to doctor images in trial and error fashion, identify another's focal points, and thereby generate images that deceived it. The modified images looked no different to human eyes. Another group showed that printouts of doctored images then photographed successfully tricked an image classification system.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:4-290>) One defense is reverse image search, in which a possible fake image is submitted to a site such as [TinEye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/TinEye> "TinEye") that can then find other instances of it. A refinement is to search using only parts of the image, to identify images from which that piece may have been taken**.**[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-291>)
Another group showed that certain [psychedelic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Psychedelic_art> "Psychedelic art") spectacles could fool a [facial recognition system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Facial_recognition_system> "Facial recognition system") into thinking ordinary people were celebrities, potentially allowing one person to impersonate another. In 2017 researchers added stickers to [stop signs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Stop_sign> "Stop sign") and caused an ANN to misclassify them.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:4-290>)
ANNs can however be further trained to detect attempts at [deception](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Deception> "Deception"), potentially leading attackers and defenders into an arms race similar to the kind that already defines the [malware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Malware> "Malware") defense industry. ANNs have been trained to defeat ANN-based anti-[malware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Malware> "Malware") software by repeatedly attacking a defense with malware that was continually altered by a [genetic algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Genetic_algorithm> "Genetic algorithm") until it tricked the anti-malware while retaining its ability to damage the target.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:4-290>)
In 2016, another group demonstrated that certain sounds could make the [Google Now](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Google_Now> "Google Now") voice command system open a particular web address, and hypothesized that this could "serve as a stepping stone for further attacks (e.g., opening a web page hosting drive-by malware)".[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:4-290>)
In "[data poisoning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Adversarial_machine_learning#Data_poisoning> "Adversarial machine learning")", false data is continually smuggled into a machine learning system's training set to prevent it from achieving mastery.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:4-290>)
### Data collection ethics
[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</w/index.php?title=Deep_learning&action=edit&section=39> "Edit section: Data collection ethics")]
The deep learning systems that are trained using supervised learning often rely on data that is created or annotated by humans, or both.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-292>) It has been argued that not only low-paid [clickwork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Clickworkers> "Clickworkers") (such as on [Amazon Mechanical Turk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Amazon_Mechanical_Turk> "Amazon Mechanical Turk")) is regularly deployed for this purpose, but also implicit forms of human [microwork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Microwork> "Microwork") that are often not recognized as such.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:13-293>) The philosopher [Rainer Mühlhoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Rainer_M%C3%BChlhoff> "Rainer Mühlhoff") distinguishes five types of "machinic capture" of human microwork to generate training data: (1) [gamification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Gamification> "Gamification") (the embedding of annotation or computation tasks in the flow of a game), (2) "trapping and tracking" (e.g. [CAPTCHAs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/CAPTCHA> "CAPTCHA") for image recognition or click-tracking on Google [search results pages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Search_engine_results_page> "Search engine results page")), (3) exploitation of social motivations (e.g. [tagging faces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Tag_\(Facebook\)> "Tag \(Facebook\)") on [Facebook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Facebook> "Facebook") to obtain labeled facial images), (4) [information mining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Information_mining> "Information mining") (e.g. by leveraging [quantified-self](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Quantified_self> "Quantified self") devices such as [activity trackers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Activity_tracker> "Activity tracker")) and (5) [clickwork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Clickworkers> "Clickworkers").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/<#cite_note-:13-293>)

[Artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Artificial_intelligence> "Artificial intelligence") (AI)  
---  
[History](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/History_of_artificial_intelligence> "History of artificial intelligence") ([timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Timeline_of_artificial_intelligence> "Timeline of artificial intelligence"))

Architectures| 
  * [Neural Turing machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Neural_Turing_machine> "Neural Turing machine")

  * [Long short-term memory (LSTM)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Long_short-term_memory> "Long short-term memory")
  * [Gated recurrent unit (GRU)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Gated_recurrent_unit> "Gated recurrent unit")
  * [Echo state network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Echo_state_network> "Echo state network")
  * [Multilayer perceptron (MLP)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Multilayer_perceptron> "Multilayer perceptron")
  * [Convolutional neural network (CNN)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Convolutional_neural_network> "Convolutional neural network")
  * [Residual neural network (RNN)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Residual_neural_network> "Residual neural network")
  * [Highway network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Highway_network> "Highway network")
  * [Mamba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Mamba_\(deep_learning_architecture\)> "Mamba \(deep learning architecture\)")
  * [Autoencoder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Autoencoder> "Autoencoder")
  * [Variational autoencoder (VAE)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Variational_autoencoder> "Variational autoencoder")
  * [Generative adversarial network (GAN)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Generative_adversarial_network> "Generative adversarial network")
  * [Graph neural network (GNN)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/</wiki/Graph_neural_network> "Graph neural network")
